<div id="review_146132327" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146132327" />
    <a title="Williwaw" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3491750-williwaw"><img alt="Williwaw" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304797883p2/3491750.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/146132327?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Williwaw" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Williwaw" href="/user/show/3491750-williwaw">Williwaw</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345021991" href="/book/show/1407134.More_Than_Human">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146132327" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9060873221573641715">I thought I had already reviewed this!<br/><br/>Perhaps not. <br/><br/>It's difficult to decide if this book (a "fix-up" novel) deserves 4 or 5 stars. Sometimes, Sturgeon's style reminds me of passages in Faulkner's Sound and Fury, when Faulkner is writing from a child's perspective. Other times, it's like he's channeling J.D. Salinger.<br/><br/>Initially, Sturgeon wrote a story called "Baby is Three," published in Galaxy Science Fiction in the early 1950s. That story is the heart of the novel, and the most engaging part of </span>
  <span id="freeText9060873221573641715" style="display:none">I thought I had already reviewed this!<br /><br />Perhaps not. <br /><br />It's difficult to decide if this book (a "fix-up" novel) deserves 4 or 5 stars. Sometimes, Sturgeon's style reminds me of passages in Faulkner's Sound and Fury, when Faulkner is writing from a child's perspective. Other times, it's like he's channeling J.D. Salinger.<br /><br />Initially, Sturgeon wrote a story called "Baby is Three," published in Galaxy Science Fiction in the early 1950s. That story is the heart of the novel, and the most engaging part of it. The setting of "Baby is Three" is a psychoanalyst's office. A back-story unfolds as part of the dialog between the patient (a shrewd young boy with a very unusual problem) and the analyst. <br /><br />Sturgeon sandwiched "Baby is Three" between two additional sequences in order to to expand it into a novel. <br /><br />I believe that this book has universal appeal. It's very emotionally charged, and the characters are easy to relate to, despite the fact that they are what we might call idiot savants: people with deep flaws but paranormal talents. The basic premise is that these flawed humans can come together to form a "homo gestalt," a unitary being which is greater than the sum of its parts. <br /><br />Although "More Than Human" is a science fiction/fantasy book, it is also much more than a simple genre piece. The first half builds into the fantastic and speculative themes so slowly that one barely notices it. Ultimately, the best thing about "More Than Human" is that it is so very human! <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9060873221573641715" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1913220848" />
    <a title="Lena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35645863-lena"><img alt="Lena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412534810p2/35645863.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1913220848?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lena" href="/user/show/35645863-lena">Lena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781481568401" href="/book/show/31142650-more-than-human">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Lena by: </span>
      Science Fiction Aficionados BOM
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35645863-lena?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35645863-lena?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35645863-lena?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35645863-lena?shelf=hugo">hugo</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1913220848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3498802465868664057"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490207606i/22291532._SX540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>The first Gestalt character I had ever read was in Daniel O'Malley's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1636020325?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Rook</a>. I was completely blown away by this odd and frightful concept, the sheer alienness in human form. O'Malley's Gestalt was born quadruplets (three male, one female), all mentally one organism. It (them?) was an amazing fighter as it could coordinate four separate bodies as easily you coordinate four separate limbs. <br/><br/>Part of the joy of reading Classics is learning where your favorite contemporary authors got their ideas.</span>
  <span id="freeText3498802465868664057" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490207606i/22291532._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The first Gestalt character I had ever read was in Daniel O'Malley's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1636020325?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rook</a>. I was completely blown away by this odd and frightful concept, the sheer alienness in human form. O'Malley's Gestalt was born quadruplets (three male, one female), all mentally one organism. It (them?) was an amazing fighter as it could coordinate four separate bodies as easily you coordinate four separate limbs. <br><br>Part of the joy of reading Classics is learning where your favorite contemporary authors got their ideas. O'Malley certainly read Sturgeon. <br><br>The most fascinating concept Sturgeon raised is if perhaps special needs people are meant to be part of a greater whole. Maybe instead of our norm of uniform circles and squares they are jigsaw pieces, never meant to function individually. What if they were a piece of the next stage of evolution, homogestalt, just awaiting connection?<br><br>This might have all sounded like communist propaganda in the 1950s but today it's speculation science fiction you can sink your teeth into.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3498802465868664057" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1955268661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5522571011690086472">Hmmmm, I'm torn between 3 or 4 stars. I liked how imaginative the book was for its time, I liked the characters' abilities and how everything kept coming back around to them. I liked their creative use of their powers to create their own reality and bend things to suit themselves. That was pretty intense what Gerry did to Hip, messed up, but really creative. But what I felt made the story drag a bit was how a new point in the story begins with new characters and you don't see the tie-in back to </span>
  <span id="freeText5522571011690086472" style="display:none">Hmmmm, I'm torn between 3 or 4 stars. I liked how imaginative the book was for its time, I liked the characters' abilities and how everything kept coming back around to them. I liked their creative use of their powers to create their own reality and bend things to suit themselves. That was pretty intense what Gerry did to Hip, messed up, but really creative. But what I felt made the story drag a bit was how a new point in the story begins with new characters and you don't see the tie-in back to the original story line for quite a while. You read and think why should I care what happens to some farmer? Or who is this Ms. Kew and how does she even know Lone? Eventually, it's explained. But I just thought those parts could have been trimmed down just a smidge.<br /><br />Overall, I did like the book and am glad I read it. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It raises the question of whether an ethos is really needed for Homo Gestalt if the "head" happens to be someone who isn't a simpleton or sociopath. But then, would Homo Gestalt form at all if the "head" did have a conscience? And really, is sociopath even the correct term? Because towards the end, Gerry does admit to feeling shame, which a true sociopath would be incapable of. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> What an interesting book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5522571011690086472" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_114731617" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/114731617" />
    <a title="Shira and Ari Evergreen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/837382-shira-and-ari-evergreen"><img alt="Shira and Ari Evergreen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1224596787p2/837382.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/114731617?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shira and Ari Evergreen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shira and Ari Evergreen" href="/user/show/837382-shira-and-ari-evergreen">Shira and Ari Evergreen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/837382-shira-and-ari-evergreen?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer114731617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16139522153637415323">"More Than Human" is well-intentioned, but out-dated. Sturgeon fancies that the next step in human evolution will be multicultural, but unfortunately he also envisions it as hierarchical, run by smart white men. The only two people of color are a set of identical twin black girls who can only speak one or two words and who are always (for sci fi reasons of course) naked. When the white guy finishes using their (admittedly awesome) skills he says "beat it." I'm sure that at the time, this didn't </span>
  <span id="freeText16139522153637415323" style="display:none">"More Than Human" is well-intentioned, but out-dated. Sturgeon fancies that the next step in human evolution will be multicultural, but unfortunately he also envisions it as hierarchical, run by smart white men. The only two people of color are a set of identical twin black girls who can only speak one or two words and who are always (for sci fi reasons of course) naked. When the white guy finishes using their (admittedly awesome) skills he says "beat it." I'm sure that at the time, this didn't come off as totally oppressive, since this guy was pointedly waaaay less racist than the other people in the society around him, in the book. However, reading it today is uncomfortable and disappointing.<br /><br />So, I don't really recommend this one, unless you're very interested in gestalt theory, paranormal abilities, hive or group minds, the future of human evolution, or, I dunno... sci fi novels of historic interest which are well-intentioned and progressive for their time, but unfortunately racist by today's standards? If that sounds interesting (or perhaps of some scholarly value), read this. Otherwise, skip it and find something by Ursula K. LeGuin or Octavia Butler.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16139522153637415323" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1508045357" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1508045357" />
    <a title="Chris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/93902-chris"><img alt="Chris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492541786p2/93902.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1508045357?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris" href="/user/show/93902-chris">Chris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1508045357" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11466044940442558355">Y'know, More Than Human is a decent piece of writing - but it's a very awkward read, and unfortunately dated. I like Sturgeon's stuff - I think he was on the cusp of being something truly different and revolutionary. More Than Human, in fact, probably was pretty revolutionary at the time of its publication... but, how many bizarre comic books and pulp novels have we seen on the same topic since then? Let's just say it's no longer the same groundbreaking material. <br/><br/>So, clearly, I don't blame Sturg</span>
  <span id="freeText11466044940442558355" style="display:none">Y'know, More Than Human is a decent piece of writing - but it's a very awkward read, and unfortunately dated. I like Sturgeon's stuff - I think he was on the cusp of being something truly different and revolutionary. More Than Human, in fact, probably was pretty revolutionary at the time of its publication... but, how many bizarre comic books and pulp novels have we seen on the same topic since then? Let's just say it's no longer the same groundbreaking material. <br /><br />So, clearly, I don't blame Sturgeon for my finding his novel dated. It's just a timing thing. I actually liked parts 1 &amp; 2 quite a lot... But the whole coming into a larger community and the evolution of a new species just didn't seem like it had adequate foundation or justification. It was abrupt. And it didn't feel all that interesting just yet. I wanted more personal detail and narrative. The characters were excellent - I found them so much more compelling than I did the abrupt strangeness of the conclusion. Bit of a disappointment, that. <br /><br />Anyway, More Than Human is okay. I wouldn't recommend against reading it, but I'd rather have read some more Philip K Dick.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11466044940442558355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1966382657" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1966382657" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7891507-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443344607p2/7891507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1966382657?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/7891507-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7891507-rose?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1966382657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10393357791745061689">I liked it but I thought there would be more to this story than there was.<br/><br/>Written back in the 50's, so it's a bit dated but not so much you can't enjoy it, this is the story of the evolution of the human race. We've just begun to move away from being a solitary creature to one where a group comes together to act as one. Each has powers that add to the whole, one is incredibly brilliant, twins who can transport themselves, a boy who can influence your thought and make you do things or forget thin</span>
  <span id="freeText10393357791745061689" style="display:none">I liked it but I thought there would be more to this story than there was.<br /><br />Written back in the 50's, so it's a bit dated but not so much you can't enjoy it, this is the story of the evolution of the human race. We've just begun to move away from being a solitary creature to one where a group comes together to act as one. Each has powers that add to the whole, one is incredibly brilliant, twins who can transport themselves, a boy who can influence your thought and make you do things or forget things, etc. This is the story of how they came together and learned what they can do as a group. <br /><br />The book ends right at a big revelation to the group. A good ending but if this were written today, that would have been the end of the first in a series. You could really write the hell out of a set up like this one. I'm almost surprised someone hasn't picked up where Sturgeon left off...or rewritten it to bring it up to date. I wonder if Scalzi's read this one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10393357791745061689" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_84603020" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/84603020" />
    <a title="Addie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1689574-addie"><img alt="Addie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516329300p2/1689574.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/84603020?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Addie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Addie" href="/user/show/1689574-addie">Addie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer84603020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2200208444786118030">Not an easy read for me. Extremely well-written with incredibly brilliant concepts, but difficult to wrap my brain around completely. There were many passages that I had to reread three or four times. A fair bit of the narrative seemed to go over my head, and I have to admit that there were a few times that I thought maybe I was not smart enough to fully appreciate this book. But then, inevitably, everything would come to light and I came out of my confusion right alongside the characters.<br/><br/>Origin</span>
  <span id="freeText2200208444786118030" style="display:none">Not an easy read for me. Extremely well-written with incredibly brilliant concepts, but difficult to wrap my brain around completely. There were many passages that I had to reread three or four times. A fair bit of the narrative seemed to go over my head, and I have to admit that there were a few times that I thought maybe I was not smart enough to fully appreciate this book. But then, inevitably, everything would come to light and I came out of my confusion right alongside the characters.<br /><br />Original and intriguing, I will be thinking about this book for some time. <br /><br />I would like to own a copy of this book so that I may study it in-depth in the future. More Than Human has all the right pieces to become a favorite book of mine, but I think it may take a while for me to understand the awesome concepts put forth by Sturgeon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2200208444786118030" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('D7Ur7hQEzwV/beLC4gVdl6DyUBdoHqs3ODEeCXqSZ4aen8uof6cUhaqlcw4+wm9dls7ETjMx3LBY/0ghJVMhiw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('87+lZmqcggaeUJucVT333sMKf+b+On11w+0CRnj9GSVilUUgAT9ZhkuYClCJ+sUU9Tbrv6UVCvKjI1RuJzxfKA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14339314248999619873">Theodore Sturgeon (1918–1985) is considered one of the godfathers of contemporary science fiction and dark fantasy. The author of numerous acclaimed short stories and novels, among them the classics More Than Human, Venus Plus X, and To Marry Medusa, Sturgeon also wrote for television and holds among his credits two episodes of the original 1960s Star Trek series, for which he created the Vulcan m</span>
  <span id="freeText14339314248999619873" style="display:none">Theodore Sturgeon (1918–1985) is considered one of the godfathers of contemporary science fiction and dark fantasy. The author of numerous acclaimed short stories and novels, among them the classics More Than Human, Venus Plus X, and To Marry Medusa, Sturgeon also wrote for television and holds among his credits two episodes of the original 1960s Star Trek series, for which he created the Vulcan mating ritual and the expression “Live long and prosper.” He is also credited as the inspiration for Kurt Vonnegut’s recurring fictional character Kilgore Trout. <br /><br />Sturgeon is the recipient of the Hugo Award, the Nebula Award, and the International Fantasy Award. In 2000, he was posthumously honored with a World Fantasy Award for Life Achievement. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14339314248999619873" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
